            function wpSolutionToggle(solution, link, showtext, hidetext) {
                if (solution.style.display != 'none') {
                    solution.style.display = 'none';
                    link.innerHTML = showtext;
                    link.className = 'solution_link_show';
                } else {
                    solution.style.display = 'block';
                    link.innerHTML = hidetext;
                    link.className = 'solution_link_hide';
                }
            }

<script type="text/javascript">
//<![CDATA[



/* JQUERY */
jQuery(document).ready(function(){ 
    
   
  

	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish(); */
	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish().find('ul').bgIframe({opacity:false}); */
 
	/* For IE6 */
	if (jQuery.browser.msie && /MSIE 6\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 7\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 8\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent)) {

		/* Max-width for images in IE6 */		
		var centerwidth = jQuery("td#middle").width(); 
		
		/* Images without caption */
		jQuery(".post img").each(function() { 
			var maxwidth = centerwidth - 10 + 'px';
			var imgwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var imgheight = jQuery(this).height(); 
			var newimgheight = (centerwidth / imgwidth * imgheight) + 'px';	
			if (imgwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxwidth}); 
				jQuery(this).css({height: newimgheight}); 
			}
		});
		
		/* Images with caption */
		jQuery("div.wp-caption").each(function() { 
			var captionwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var maxcaptionwidth = centerwidth + 'px';
			var captionheight = jQuery(this).height();
			var captionimgwidth =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").width();
			var captionimgheight =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").height();
			if (captionwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxcaptionwidth}); 
				var newcaptionheight = (centerwidth / captionwidth * captionheight) + 'px';
				var newcaptionimgheight = (centerwidth / captionimgwidth * captionimgheight) + 'px';
				jQuery(this).css({height: newcaptionheight}); 
				jQuery("div.wp-caption img").css({height: newcaptionimgheight}); 
				}
		});
		
		/* sfhover for LI:HOVER support in IE6: */
		jQuery("ul li").
			hover( function() {
					jQuery(this).addClass("sfhover")
				}, 
				function() {
					jQuery(this).removeClass("sfhover")
				} 
			); 

	/* End IE6 */
	}
	
	
	
	/* Since 3.7.8: Auto resize videos (embed and iframe elements) 
	TODO: Parse parent's dimensions only once per layout column, not per video
	*/
	function bfa_resize_video() {
		jQuery('embed, iframe').each( function() {
			var video = jQuery(this),
			videoWidth = video.attr('width'); // use the attr here, not width() or css()
			videoParent = video.parent(),
			videoParentWidth = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'width' ) ),
			videoParentBorder = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-left-width' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-right-width' ) ),
			videoParentPadding = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-left' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-right' ) ),
			maxWidth = videoParentWidth - videoParentBorder - videoParentPadding;

			if( videoWidth > maxWidth ) {
				var videoHeight = video.attr('height'),
				videoMaxHeight = ( maxWidth / videoWidth * videoHeight );
				video.attr({ width: maxWidth, height: videoMaxHeight });
			} 

		});	
	}
	bfa_resize_video();
	jQuery(window).resize( bfa_resize_video );

		
	jQuery(".post table tr").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("over");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("over");
		});

	
	jQuery(".post table tr:even").
		addClass("alt");

	
	jQuery("input.text, input.TextField, input.file, input.password, textarea").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("highlight"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("highlight"); 
		})
	
	jQuery("input.inputblur").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("inputfocus"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("inputfocus"); 
		})

		

	
	jQuery("input.button, input.Button, input#submit").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("buttonhover");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("buttonhover");
		});

	/* toggle "you can use these xhtml tags" */
	jQuery("a.xhtmltags").
		click(function(){ 
			jQuery("div.xhtml-tags").slideToggle(300); 
		});

	/* For the Tabbed Widgets plugin: */
	jQuery("ul.tw-nav-list").
		addClass("clearfix");

		
	
});

//]]>
</script>

src="http://pagead2.googlesyndication.com/pagead/show_ads.js">

</div></div>	
								<div class="post-70 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-cpp-tutorial odd" id="post-70">
						<div class="post-headline">		<h1>4.7 &#8212; Structs</h1>
		</div>		<div class="post-byline">By Alex, on June 20th, 2007</div>		<div class="post-bodycopy clearfix"><p>There are many instances in programming where we need more than one variable in order to represent an object.  For example, to represent yourself, you might want to store your name, your birthday, your height, your weight, or any other number of characteristics about yourself.  You could do so like this:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d58880300103249" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d58880300103249-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d58880300103249-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d58880300103249-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d58880300103249-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d58880300103249-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d58880300103249-6">6</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d58880300103249-1"><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-t">string</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">myName</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d58880300103249-2"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">myBirthYear</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d58880300103249-3"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">myBirthMonth</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d58880300103249-4"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">myBirthDay</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d58880300103249-5"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">myHeightInches</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d58880300103249-6"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">myWeightPounds</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0010 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>However, you now have 6 independent variables that are not grouped in any way.  If you wanted to pass information about yourself to a function, you&#8217;d have to pass each variable individually.  Furthermore, if you wanted to store information about someone else, you&#8217;d have to declare 6 more variables for each additional person!  As you can see, this can quickly get out of control.</p>
<p>Fortunately, C++ allows us to create our own user-defined aggregate data types.  An <strong>aggregate data type</strong> is a data type that groups multiple individual variables together.  One of the simplest aggregate data type is the struct.  A <strong>struct</strong> (short for structure) allows us to group variables of mixed data types together into a single unit.</p>
<p><strong>Declaring and defining structs</strong></p>
<p>Because structs are user-defined, we first have to tell the compiler what our struct looks like before we can begin using it.  To do this, we declare our struct using the <em>struct</em> keyword.  Here is an example of a struct declaration:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d58893089730983" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d58893089730983-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d58893089730983-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d58893089730983-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d58893089730983-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d58893089730983-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d58893089730983-6">6</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d58893089730983-1"><span class="crayon-t">struct</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">Employee</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d58893089730983-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d58893089730983-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">short</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">id</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d58893089730983-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">age</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d58893089730983-5"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">double</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">wage</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d58893089730983-6"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0007 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This tells the compiler that we are defining a struct named Employee.  The Employee struct contains 3 variables inside of it: a short named id, an int named age, and a double named wage.  These variables that are part of the struct are called <strong>members</strong> (or fields).  Keep in mind that Employee is just a declaration -- even though we are telling the compiler that the struct will have variables, no memory is allocated at this time.  By convention, struct names start with a capital letter to distinguish them from variable names.</p>
<table border=1 cellspacing=0 cellpadding=3 width=100%>
<tr>
<td>
Warning: One of the easiest mistakes to make in C++ is to forget the semicolon at the end of a struct declaration.  This will cause a compiler error on the <em>next</em> line of code.  Modern compilers like Visual Studio 2010 will give you an indication that you may have forgotten a semicolon, but older or less sophisticated compilers may not, which can make the actual error hard to find.
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In order to use the Employee struct, we simply declare a variable of type Employee:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d5889b489303301" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5889b489303301-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d5889b489303301-1"><span class="crayon-e">Employee </span><span class="crayon-v">joe</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// struct Employee is capitalized, variable joe is not</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0003 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This defines a variable of type Employee named joe.  As with normal variables, defining a struct variable allocates memory for that variable.</p>
<p>It is possible to define multiple variables of the same struct type:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d588a2941486666" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588a2941486666-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588a2941486666-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588a2941486666-1"><span class="crayon-e">Employee </span><span class="crayon-v">joe</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// create an Employee struct for Joe</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d588a2941486666-2"><span class="crayon-e">Employee </span><span class="crayon-v">frank</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// create an Employee struct for Frank</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0005 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p><strong>Accessing struct members</strong></p>
<p>When we define a variable such as <code>Employee joe</code>, joe refers to the entire struct (which contains the member variables).  In order to access the individual members, we use the <strong>member selection operator</strong> (which is a period).  Here is an example of using the member selection operator to initialize each member variable:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-6">6</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-7">7</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-8">8</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-9">9</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-1"><span class="crayon-e">Employee </span><span class="crayon-v">joe</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// create an Employee struct for Joe</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-2"><span class="crayon-v">joe</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">id</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">14</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// assign a value to member id within struct joe</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-3"><span class="crayon-v">joe</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">age</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">32</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// assign a value to member age within struct joe</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-4"><span class="crayon-v">joe</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">wage</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">24.15</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// assign a value to member wage within struct joe</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-5">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-6"><span class="crayon-e">Employee </span><span class="crayon-v">frank</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// create an Employee struct for Frank</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-7"><span class="crayon-v">frank</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">id</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">15</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// assign a value to member id within struct frank</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-8"><span class="crayon-v">frank</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">age</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">28</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// assign a value to member age within struct frank</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588a8669239323-9"><span class="crayon-v">frank</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">wage</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">18.27</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// assign a value to member wage within struct frank</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0021 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>As with normal variables, struct member variables are not initialized, and will typically contain junk.  We must initialize them manually.</p>
<p>In the above example, it is very easy to tell which member variables belong to Joe and which belong to Frank.  This provides a much higher level of organization than individual variables would.  Furthermore, because Joe&#8217;s and Frank&#8217;s members have the same names, this provides consistency across multiple variables of the same struct type.</p>
<p>Struct member variables act just like normal variables, so it is possible to do normal operations on them:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-6">6</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-7">7</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-8">8</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-9">9</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-10">10</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-11">11</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-12">12</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">totalAge</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">joe</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">age</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">+</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">frank</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">age</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-2">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-3"><span class="crayon-st">if</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">joe</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">wage</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&gt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">frank</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">wage</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"Joe makes more than Frank\n"</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-5"><span class="crayon-st">else</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"Joe makes less than Frank\n"</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-7">&nbsp;</div><div crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d588b0207178758-12"><span class="crayon-o">++</span><span class="crayon-v">joe</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">age</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// use pre-increment to increment Joe's age by 1</span></div></div></td>

<p></p>
<p><strong>Initializer lists</strong></p>
<p>Initializing structs by assigning values member by member is a little cumbersome, so C++ supports a faster way to initialize structs using an <strong>initializer list</strong>.  This allows you to initialize some or all the members of a struct at declaration time.</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

<p></p>

class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588bd769667270-31"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0043 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>In the above example, we pass an entire Employee struct to printInformation().  This prevents us from having to pass each variable individually.  Furthermore, if we ever decide to add new members to our Employee struct, we will not have to change the function declaration or function call!</p>
<p>The above program outputs:</p>
<pre>
ID:   14
Age:  32
Wage: 24.15

ID:   15
Age:  28
Wage: 18.27
</pre>
<p>A function can also return a struct, which is one of the few ways to have a function return multiple variables.</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">

</pre>
<p><strong>Nested structs</strong></p>
<p>Structs can contain other structs.  For example:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

<p></p>
<p>In this case, if we wanted to know what the CEO&#8217;s salary was, we simply use the member selection operator twice: <code>myCompany.CEO.wage;</code></p>
<p>This selects the CEO member from myCompany, and then selects the wage member from within CEO.</p>
<p>You can use nested initializer lists for nested structs:</p>

class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">1</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">42</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">60000.0f</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">5</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0018 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p><strong>Struct size and data structure alignment</strong></p>
<p>Typically, the size of a struct is the sum of the size of all its members, but not always!</p>
<p>Consider the Employee struct.  On many platforms, a short is 2 bytes, an int is 4 bytes, and a double is 8 bytes, so we&#8217;d expect Employee to be 2 + 4 + 8 = 14 bytes.  To find out the exact size of Employee, we can use the sizeof operator:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-6">6</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-7">7</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-8">8</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-9">9</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-10">10</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-11">11</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-12">12</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-13">13</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-1"><span class="crayon-t">struct</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">Employee</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">short</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">id</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">age</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-5"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">double</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">wage</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-6"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-7">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-8"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-9"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"The size of Employee is "</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">sizeof</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">Employee</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"\n"</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-11">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-12"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d588d8089708187-13"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0015 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>On the author&#8217;s machine, this prints:</p>
<pre>
The size of Employee is 16
</pre>
<p>It turns out, we can only say that the size of a struct will be <em>at least</em> as large as the size of all the variables it contains.  But it could be larger!  For performance reasons, the compiler will sometimes add gaps into structures (this is called <strong>padding</strong>).</p>
<p>In the Employee struct above, the compiler is invisibly adding 2 bytes of padding after member id, making the size of the structure 16 bytes instead of 14.  The reason it does this is beyond the scope of this tutorial, but readers who want to learn more can read about <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure_alignment" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_structure_alignment', 'data structure alignment']);" >data structure alignment</a> on Wikipedia.  This is optional reading and not required to understand structures or C++!</p>
<p><strong>A few final notes on structs</strong></p>
<p>Because struct declarations do not take any memory, it is common to declare structs in a header file, so they can be accessed in multiple source files.</p>
<p>Structs are <em>very</em> important in C++, as understanding structs is the first major step towards object-oriented programming!  Later on in these tutorials, you&#8217;ll learn about another aggregate data type called a class, which is built on top of structs.  Understanding structs well will help make the transition to classes that much easier.</p>
<p><strong>Quiz</strong></p>
<p>1) You are running a website, and you are trying to keep track of how much money you make per day from advertising.  Declare an advertising struct that keeps track of how many ads you&#8217;ve shown to readers, what percentage of users clicked on ads, and how much you earned on average from each ad that was clicked.  Read in values for each of these fields from the user.  Pass the advertising struct to a function that prints each of the values, and then calculates how much you made for that day (multiply all 3 fields together).</p>
<p>2) Create a struct to hold a fraction.  The struct should have a integer numerator and a integer denominator member.  Declare 2 fraction variables and read them in from the user.  Write a function called multiply that takes both fractions, multiplies them together, and prints the result out as a decimal number.  You do not need to reduce the fraction to its lowest terms.</p>

	int adv;<br />

	float click;<br />

<p>float money(int adv,float rate,float click)<br />
{<br />
	float totalearning;<br />
	totalearning = (adv * rate * click);<br />
	return totalearning;<br />
}</p>
<p>web mny;</p>
<p>void main()<br />
{<br />
	float res;</p>

	cin &gt;&gt; mny.rate;</p>
<p>	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;n Average of earning per click : &quot;;<br />

<p>	res = money(mny.adv , mny.rate , mny.click);</p>

}</p>

		<p>Is there such a thing like typedef pointers? I got into trouble to initialize PCOORD. Finally I figured it out but I am not sure that am I doing the right thing? I thought it would be good to put this code example here since the mechanism is used in many places.</p>
<p>For example (code):</p>
<p>typedef struct Coordinate<br />
{<br />
   short X;<br />
   short Y;<br />
} COORD, *PCOORD;</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
   COORD pos;<br />
   pos.X = 0;<br />
   pos.Y = 0;<br />
   PCOORD pPos = &amp;pos;<br />
}</p>
<p>At the beginning my main function looked like the main() below:</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
   //this is the wrong way to do things<br />
   PCOORD pPos;<br />
   pPos-&gt;X = 0;<br />
   pPos-&gt;Y = 0;<br />
   //if you use pPos now in somewhere compiler gives you warning that pPos is not initialized and my program crashed if I run that.<br />
   // Why is it so? Why I cant initialize?<br />
}</p>
		</div>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/?replytocom=63757#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-63757", "63757", "respond", "70" )' aria-label='Reply to Quinn'> &middot; Reply</a></span>

		<p>This is probably old but I&#8217;ll answer it anyway, for future reference.</p>
<p>ReadScore doesn&#8217;t return the s1 struct. Since s1 is declared locally in both the main function and the ReadScore function, it&#8217;s two separate Score structs. Therefore, when you called ReadScore, it didn&#8217;t change the value of main()s s1 Score struct. To change that code to work right, you&#8217;d either need to use pointers, or you could return the struct from ReadScore. The following examples exclude your other perfectly fine function and struct declaration.</p>
<p>Returning struct:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d5df6b164703710" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>

class="crayon-v">s1</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d5df6b164703710-12"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">s1</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">ReadScore</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d5df6b164703710-13"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">PrintScore</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">s1</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d5df6b164703710-14"><span class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d5df6b164703710-15"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0017 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Or you could use pointers:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d5df75435660361" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

<p>What I dont understand is, why they write &#8220;something&#8221; two times?</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-33901">
		<div id="div-comment-33901" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/#comment-33901">
		December 7, 2008 at 10:54 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/?replytocom=33901#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-33901", "33901", "respond", "70" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>It&#8217;s easier to understand when you use different labels:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d5e21b381516685" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5e21b381516685-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5e21b381516685-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5e21b381516685-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5e21b381516685-4">4</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d5e21b381516685-1"><span class="crayon-t">struct</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">something</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d5e21b381516685-2"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d5e21b381516685-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d5e21b381516685-4"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">somethingelse</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0007 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>In this case, something is the name of the struct itself.  It&#8217;s like naming a function, it&#8217;s just a label to reference it by later.  This doesn&#8217;t actually create a struct object, it just lays out what a struct looks like.</p>
<p>somethingelse declares an actual struct object.  It is a variable that takes up memory.</p>
<p>So when you see something like this:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d5e226430910318" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5e226430910318-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5e226430910318-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5e226430910318-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5e226430910318-4">4</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d5e226430910318-1"><span class="crayon-t">struct</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">something</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d5e226430910318-2"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d5e226430910318-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d5e226430910318-4"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">something</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0006 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>It basically means you&#8217;re defining a struct named something, and then also defining a local variable with the same name.  In my opinion, this is bad coding style since you&#8217;re using the same name for two different things.</p>
<p>Usually when I see this, it&#8217;s because people want a &#8220;one off&#8221; struct -- something that&#8217;s only used once.  In that case, you can just use an anonymous struct:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d5e22d455133605" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5e22d455133605-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5e22d455133605-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5e22d455133605-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5e22d455133605-4">4</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d5e22d455133605-1"><span class="crayon-t">struct</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d5e22d455133605-2"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d5e22d455133605-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d743d5e22d455133605-4"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">something</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0006 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This struct has no name and the type can never be referenced directly.  However, something is a variable of that type.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/?replytocom=53039#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-53039", "53039", "respond", "70" )' aria-label='Reply to manju'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>U are actually passing the structure sCEO which is not declared . So the compiler gives u an error . Since the sCEO is a member of sMyCompany. U should use sMyCompany.sCEO in order to access the structure of Employee  sCEO . </p>
<p>The following line would fix ur problem<br />
  PrintInformation(sMyCompany.sCEO);<br />
instead of<br />
  PrintInformation(sCEO);</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

		<li class="comment even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-77870">
		<div id="div-comment-77870" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/fc369c3c63d96791b1957dbd675c6045?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/fc369c3c63d96791b1957dbd675c6045?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Ole</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/#comment-77870">
		February 4, 2010 at 4:08 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/?replytocom=77870#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-77870", "77870", "respond", "70" )' aria-label='Reply to Ole'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Let me quote Alex and highligth the important bit that you wonder about:</p>
<p>&#8220;Typically, the size of a struct is the sum of the size of all its members. In this case, since each integer is 4 bytes and a float is 4 bytes, Employee would be 12 bytes. However, some platforms have specific rules about how variables must be laid out in memory  consequently, <b>the compiler may leave gaps between the variables.</b> As a result, we can say the struct will be at minimum 12 bytes.&#8221;</p>
<p>Cheers<br />
Ole</p>
		</div>

		<p>Try this:</p>
<p><code></p>
<p>#include<br />
#include </p>
<p>struct Fractions<br />
{<br />
       int nNumerator;<br />
       int nDenominator;<br />
};</p>
<p>float multiply(float x, float y)<br />
{<br />
      return x * y;<br />
}</p>
<p>float produceValue()<br />
{<br />
      using namespace std;<br />
      Fractions sAny;<br />
      cout &lt;&gt; sAny.nNumerator;<br />
      cout &lt;&gt; sAny.nDenominator;<br />
      float result = (float)sAny.nNumerator / sAny.nDenominator;<br />
      return (result);<br />
}</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
      using namespace std;<br />
      cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Now, we are going to multiply two fractions. First: &quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
      float x = produceValue();<br />
      cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Now, once again &quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
      float y = produceValue();<br />
      cout &lt;&lt; &quot;The answer is &quot; &lt;&lt; multiply(x, y);<br />
      cin.clear();<br />
      cin.ignore(255, &#039;\n&#039;);<br />
      cin.get();<br />
      return 0;<br />
}<br />
</code><code></code></p>

		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0046 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>What happens is that when you run through the function Read() it stores the data in the SCOPE, and than is destroyed after the function ends. So when you return scompany and store it into scompany on int main(), it passes the values to the main() scope. There might be a little more to it but basically the values are destroyed when Read() ends so you have to pass it on to main() which I have done. BTW I am unsure as to why you included stdafx.h when you have nothing in your program that needs that header, whats even more curious is the way you included it (with &#8220;&#8221; instead of ) and that it compiled at all.</p>
		</div>

		</div>
		<p>In your &#8220;Quiz 1 Answer&#8221; You did not divide the percentage, or at least turn it into a decimal, so the output will be wrong.</p>
<p>For example:</p>
<p>5000 * 50 * $.15 = $37,500<br />
5000 * (50 / 100) * $.15 = $375</p>
<p>The two are very different. The user will not know to put a decimal instead of a whole number (in fact they might even put a modulus after the number which is bad). I guess I am just a little nit-picky. BTW here is my answer if you are interested:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<p>The way the problem was originally specified asked the user to enter a percentage as a number between 0 and 1, so the division by 100 wasn&#8217;t necessary.  But I think more people probably think about percentages the way you do (between 0 and 100 instead of between 0 and 1), so I&#8217;ve altered the question and answer.</p>

		<div id="div-comment-91179" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/bf6a79276532ceb36c6571caf682944f?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/bf6a79276532ceb36c6571caf682944f?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">JD</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/#comment-91179">
		August 31, 2010 at 12:49 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/?replytocom=91179#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-91179", "91179", "respond", "70" )' aria-label='Reply to JD'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>I kinda doubt you&#8217;re still wondering this 2 months later, but in case you haven&#8217;t figured it out:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d5d3cc657299310" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5d3cc657299310-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d5d3cc657299310-1"><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">static_cast</span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;</span><span class="crayon-t">float</span><span class="crayon-o">&gt;</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">numerator</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">/</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">denominator</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0005 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Because the / operator is in the parenthesis, the division is performed first.  Both inputs are integers, so it is performed as an integer operation (and rounded to 0).  Only after the division is complete does it convert the result to float.  You want the division to be a float operation, so you should cast one of the inputs *before* the division, as follows:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d5d3d7496350984" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5d3d7496350984-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d5d3d7496350984-1"><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">static_cast</span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;</span><span class="crayon-t">float</span><span class="crayon-o">&gt;</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">numerator</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">/</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">denominator</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0005 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This will make it a float operation, and it will not be rounded.</p>
		</div>

		<p>I&#8217;m not sure why this wouldn&#8217;t work.  You should be able to declare a struct inside a function (I tested it with Visual Studio 2010 Express and it works).</p>
<p>If you do this, the struct declaration has local scope, so you&#8217;ll only be able to create variables of this struct type within that function.</p>

<p>#include &#8220;stdafx.h&#8221;<br />

{<br />
	int nNumerator;<br />
	int nDenomintor;<br />
};</p>
<p>double Input()<br />
{<br />
	using namespace std;<br />
	Fraction sFrac;<br />

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-252322">
		<div id="div-comment-252322" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/#comment-252322">
		May 2, 2015 at 10:01 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/?replytocom=252322#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252322", "252322", "respond", "70" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Because you&#8217;re doing integer division and casting the result to a float instead of doing floating point division.</p>
<p>Instead of:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d743d5c521808924841" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d743d5c521808924841-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d743d5c521808924841-1"><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">static_cast</span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;</span><span class="crayon-t">float</span><span class="crayon-o">&gt;</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">sFrac</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">nNumerator</span><span class="crayon-o">/</span><span class="crayon-v">sFrac</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">nDenomintor</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>

			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0006 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>try:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<p>Just thought I&#8217;d share my code like some people are:</p>
<p>First exercise, in main.cpp:<br />
<code>#include &lt;iostream&gt;<br />
#include &quot;main.h&quot;</p>
<p>using namespace std;</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
    cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Hi there!  Um, please enter the following:\n&quot; &lt;&lt;<br />
            &quot;-- Total ads shown to users\n&quot; &lt;&lt;<br />
            &quot;-- Percent of ads clicked\n&quot; &lt;&lt;<br />
            &quot;-- Average profit per ad&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
    Advertising sAds;<br />
    cin &gt;&gt;  sAds.nAdsShown &gt;&gt;<br />
            sAds.fPercentClicked &gt;&gt;<br />
            sAds.fAverageProfit;<br />
    sAds.fPercentClicked /= 100;    // Convert from percent to decimal so next calculation can occur<br />
    cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Total profit today: $&quot; &lt;&lt;<br />
            (<br />
                sAds.nAdsShown *<br />
                sAds.fPercentClicked *<br />
                sAds.fAverageProfit<br />
            ) &lt;&lt; endl;</p>
<p>}</code></p>
<p>First exercise, main.h:<br />
<code>#ifndef MAIN_H<br />
#define MAIN_H</p>
<p>struct Advertising<br />
{<br />
    int nAdsShown;<br />
    float fPercentClicked;<br />
    float fAverageProfit;<br />
};</p>
<p>#endif</code></p>
<p>Second exercise, main.cpp:<br />
<code>#include &lt;iostream&gt;<br />
#include &quot;main.h&quot;</p>
<p>using namespace std;</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
    Fraction sMyFrac, sYourFrac;<br />
    cin &gt;&gt; sMyFrac.nNumer &gt;&gt; sMyFrac.nDenom;<br />
    cin &gt;&gt; sYourFrac.nNumer &gt;&gt; sYourFrac.nDenom;<br />
    Fraction sProduct = multFractions(sMyFrac, sYourFrac);<br />
    printFraction(sProduct);<br />
}</p>
<p>Fraction multFractions(Fraction sX, Fraction sY)<br />
{<br />
    Fraction sProduct;<br />
    sProduct.nNumer = sX.nNumer * sY.nNumer;<br />
    sProduct.nDenom = sX.nDenom * sY.nDenom;<br />
    return sProduct;<br />
    //return (new Fraction{sX.nNumer * sY.nNumer, sX.nDenom * sY.nDenom}); // one-liner?<br />
}</p>
<p>void printFraction(Fraction sFrac)<br />
{<br />
    cout &lt;&lt; static_cast&lt;double&gt;(sFrac.nNumer) / sFrac.nDenom;<br />
}</code></p>
<p>Second exercise, main.h:<br />
<code>#ifndef MAIN_H<br />
#define MAIN_H</p>
<p>struct Fraction<br />
{<br />
    int nNumer;<br />
    int nDenom;<br />
};</p>
<p>Fraction multFractions(Fraction sX, Fraction sY);<br />
void printFraction(Fraction sFrac);</p>
<p>#endif</code></p>

		<p>My results:</p>
<p><b>main.cpp</b><br />
<code><br />
#include &lt;iostream&gt;<br />
#include &quot;functions2.h&quot;<br />
using namespace std;</p>
<p>advertising campaign1;<br />
fraction frac1, frac2;</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
	campaign1 = getData(campaign1);<br />
	printResults(campaign1);</p>
<p>	cout &lt;&lt; endl &lt;&lt; &quot;NEXT PART OF THE EXERCISE!&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;</p>
<p>	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;First fraction&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
	frac1 = getFrac(frac1);<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Second fraction&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
	frac2 = getFrac(frac2);<br />
	fracProduct(frac1, frac2);</p>
<p>	cin.get();		//for halting the program<br />
	cin.ignore();	//for halting the program<br />
	return 0;<br />
}<br />
<!--formatted--></code></p>
<p><b>functions2.cpp</b><br />
<code><br />
#include &lt;iostream&gt;<br />
#include &quot;functions2.h&quot;<br />
using namespace std;</p>
<p>advertising getData(advertising x)<br />
{<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Input the number of adds in the campaign: &quot;;<br />
	cin &gt;&gt; x.numberAdds;<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Input the hit rate of the campaign: &quot;;<br />
	cin	&gt;&gt; x.hitRatio;<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Input the average revenue per hit: &quot;;<br />
	cin	&gt;&gt; x.avgRevenuePerHit;<br />
	return x;<br />
}</p>
<p>void printResults(advertising x)<br />
{<br />
	float result = x.numberAdds*x.hitRatio*x.avgRevenuePerHit;<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; endl &lt;&lt; &quot;The campaign has resulted in a total revenue of: &quot; &lt;&lt; result &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
}</p>
<p>fraction getFrac(fraction x)<br />
{<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Input a numerator: &quot;;<br />
	cin &gt;&gt; x.numerator;<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Input a denominator: &quot;;<br />
	cin &gt;&gt; x.denominator;</p>
<p>	return x;<br />
}</p>
<p>void fracProduct(fraction x, fraction y)<br />
{<br />
	float result = static_cast&lt;float&gt;(x.numerator*y.numerator)/(x.denominator*y.denominator);</p>
<p>	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Multiplying the two fractions yields: &quot; &lt;&lt; result &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
}<br />
<!--formatted--></code></p>
<p><b>functions2.h</b><br />
<code><br />
#ifndef FUNCTIONS2_H<br />
#define FUNCTIONS2_H</p>
<p>struct advertising<br />
{<br />
	int numberAdds;<br />
	float hitRatio;<br />
	float avgRevenuePerHit;<br />
};</p>
<p>struct fraction<br />
{<br />
	int numerator;<br />
	int denominator;<br />
};</p>
<p>advertising getData(advertising x);<br />
void printResults(advertising x);<br />
fraction getFrac(fraction x);<br />
void fracProduct(fraction x, fraction y);</p>
<p>#endif<br />
</code></p>

		<p>This is how I did it. It worked perfectly. But correct me if I should have done it another way. By the way, I pre-set the values for the variables because we aren&#8217;t really getting any user data to actually calculate a result.</p>
<p>#include &#8220;stdafx.h&#8221;<br />
#include </p>
<p>using namespace std;</p>
<p>struct MoneyPerDay<br />
{<br />
	int nAdShown; // 45 Ads shown each month<br />
	long float fAdsClicked; // Amount of Ads clicked by users<br />
	long float fAmountPerClick; // Each Ad click revenue is $.10<br />
	long float nUsersPerDay;</p>
<p>};</p>
<p>void PrintMoneyEarnedPerDay(MoneyPerDay sMoneyPerDay)<br />
{<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Number of users per day:  &quot; &lt;&lt; sMoneyPerDay.nUsersPerDay &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Number of Ads shown:  &quot; &lt;&lt; sMoneyPerDay.nAdShown &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Number of Ads clicked:  &quot; &lt;&lt; sMoneyPerDay.fAdsClicked &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Amount of money per Ad click:  &quot; &lt;&lt; sMoneyPerDay.fAmountPerClick &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
}</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
	MoneyPerDay sMonday;<br />
	sMonday.nUsersPerDay = 10780;<br />
	sMonday.nAdShown = 45;<br />
	sMonday.fAdsClicked = 20;<br />
	sMonday.fAmountPerClick = .10;</p>
<p>	MoneyPerDay sTuesday;<br />
	sTuesday.nUsersPerDay = 20678;<br />
	sTuesday.nAdShown = 45;<br />
	sTuesday.fAdsClicked = 20;<br />
	sTuesday.fAmountPerClick = .10;</p>
<p>	// Prints stats for monday<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Monday stats-- &quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
	PrintMoneyEarnedPerDay(sMonday);<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;The result is:  $&quot; &lt;&lt; sMonday.nUsersPerDay / sMonday.fAdsClicked * sMonday.fAmountPerClick &lt;&lt; endl;</p>
<p>	cout &lt;&lt; &quot; &quot; &lt;&lt; endl;</p>
<p>	// Prints stats for tuesday<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Tuesday stats-- &quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
	PrintMoneyEarnedPerDay(sTuesday);<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;The result is:  $&quot; &lt;&lt; sTuesday.nUsersPerDay / sTuesday.fAdsClicked * sTuesday.fAmountPerClick &lt;&lt; endl; </p>
<p>	cout &lt;&lt; &quot; &quot; &lt;&lt; endl;</p>
<p>	return 0;<br />
}</p>
		</div>

		<p>Long float is kind of an oxymoron I think? VS2012 gives warnings: </p>
<p>nonstandard extension used : long float	c:user</p>
<p>If you meant double the size of float then use &#8216;double&#8217;, but seeing as your data doesn&#8217;t exceed a float though, just the float would&#8217;ve done. <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /></p>
<p>You didn&#8217;t need the blanks here: cout &lt;&lt; &quot; &quot; &lt;&lt; endl; // just do: cout &lt;&lt; endl;</p>
<p>Keep coding. <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /></p>

		<p>//This is how I did it. Please comment ?</p>
<p>#include<br />
using namespace std;</p>
<p>struct Adverts<br />
{<br />
   unsigned short nAdsShown;<br />
   float fClickRate;<br />
   float fAveEarnPerClick;<br />
};</p>
<p>Adverts GetAdsData()<br />
{<br />
    Adverts Ads;<br />
    cout&lt;&gt;Ads.nAdsShown;<br />
    cout&lt;&gt;Ads.fClickRate;<br />
    cout&lt;&gt;Ads.fAveEarnPerClick;<br />
       return Ads;<br />
}</p>
<p>void PrintAdsResult(Adverts Ads)<br />
{<br />
    cout&lt;&lt;&quot;Total of adverts shown:\t\t&quot;&lt;&lt;Ads.nAdsShown&lt;&lt;endl;<br />
    cout&lt;&lt;&quot;Click through rate:\t\t&quot;&lt;&lt;Ads.fClickRate&lt;&lt;endl;<br />
    cout&lt;&lt;&quot;Average earnings per click:\t&quot;&lt;&lt;Ads.fAveEarnPerClick&lt;&lt;endl;<br />
        cout&lt;&lt;&quot;Total earnings for the day:\t$&quot;&lt;&lt;Ads.nAdsShown * Ads.fClickRate * Ads.fAveEarnPerClick&lt;&lt;endl;<br />
}</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
    PrintAdsResult(GetAdsData());<br />
    return 0;</p>
<p>}</p>

		<div id="div-comment-117986" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/db31ca9cb0cb7542112af9fdb4ef2d5a?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/db31ca9cb0cb7542112af9fdb4ef2d5a?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Zidane</span>

				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/#comment-117986">
		January 12, 2014 at 5:30 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/?replytocom=117986#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-117986", "117986", "respond", "70" )' aria-label='Reply to Zidane'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>#include<br />
using namespace std;</p>
<p>struct Fraction<br />
{<br />
   unsigned short nNumerator;<br />
   unsigned short nDenominator;<br />
};</p>
<p>Fraction GetFractionData()<br />
{<br />
    Fraction Fra;<br />
    static int c=1;                // &#8216;c&#8217; is a Fraction Identifier<br />
    cout&lt;&lt;&quot;Fraction &quot;&lt;&lt;c++&lt;&lt;endl;<br />
    cout&lt;&gt;Fra.nNumerator;<br />
    cout&lt;&gt;Fra.nDenominator;</p>
<p>    return Fra;<br />
}</p>
<p>void PrintMultiplyFractions(Fraction x, Fraction y)<br />
{<br />
   cout&lt;&lt;x.nNumerator&lt;&lt;&quot;/&quot;&lt;&lt;x.nDenominator&lt;&lt;<br />
   &quot; * &quot;&lt;&lt;<br />
   y.nNumerator&lt;&lt;&quot;/&quot;&lt;&lt;y.nDenominator&lt;&lt;<br />
   &quot; = &quot;&lt;&lt;<br />
   (static_cast(x.nNumerator * y.nNumerator)/(x.nDenominator * y.nDenominator))&lt;&lt;<br />
   endl;<br />
}</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
    PrintMultiplyFractions(GetFractionData(),GetFractionData());<br />
    return 0;</p>
<p>}</p>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/?replytocom=124941#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-124941", "124941", "respond", "70" )' aria-label='Reply to Arthur_'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Why do you (for the second question) declare the numerator and denominators as integers when you know you are going to need them as floats later? Wouldn&#8217;t it be more logical to declare them as floats or longs and then you don&#8217;t have to static_cast them later?</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-252326">
		<div id="div-comment-252326" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/#comment-252326">
		May 2, 2015 at 10:13 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/?replytocom=252326#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252326", "252326", "respond", "70" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>In standard mathematics, the numerators and denominators in fractions are always defined as integers.  It&#8217;s better to have your code represent mathematical convention and do the conversions when necessary than to do something non-standard for the sake of avoiding a couple of static_casts.</p>
<p>Plus using floating point numbers would allow you to define fractions like 3.4 / 10.2.  Although technically this works (and is equivalent to 1 / 3), we don&#8217;t fraction that way. <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /></p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

		<p>I managed to get my solution to question 2 correct.  Initially though I had this code inside my multiply function.</p>
<p>cout &lt;&lt; static_cast((sF1.numerator)/(sF1.denominator))*((sF2.numerator)/(sF2.denominator));</p>
<p>The program ran and compiled fine but performed integer division when I entered 1/5 * 1/1 in order to test the program, giving an answer of 0 instead of 0.2.</p>
<p>When I re-ordered that line of code to</p>
<p>cout &lt;&lt; static_cast((sF1.numerator)*(sF2.numerator))/((sF1.denominator)*(sF2.denominator));</p>
<p>the program works fine and performs the division properly, giving the correct answer (0.2).</p>
<p>Why is this, to me the functions perform the same operations, am I missing something obvious?</p>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-252327">
		<div id="div-comment-252327" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/#comment-252327">
		May 2, 2015 at 10:17 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/?replytocom=252327#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252327", "252327", "respond", "70" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>In the first line, you&#8217;re doing integer division and casting the integer result to a float (which is useless).</p>
<p>In the second line, you&#8217;re casting the first operand to a float, which causes the division operator to convert the second operand to a float as well, and do floating point division.</p>
		</div>
