		<p>I completed question 2 slightly differently, it works fine and gives the correct results. Have I done anything that would be considered bad practice or is this OK?&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
<p>[#include &quot;stdafx.h&quot;<br />
#include &lt;iostream&gt;</p>
<p>struct FRACTION<br />
{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;int numer_one;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;int numer_two;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;int denom_one;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;int denom_two;<br />
};</p>
<p>void fractionMultiplied(FRACTION fraction)<br />
{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;using namespace std;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// fraction multiplication<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;float numer_sum = fraction.numer_one * fraction.numer_two;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;float denom_sum = fraction.denom_one * fraction.denom_two;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;float decemal_output = numer_sum / denom_sum;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; &quot;The decimal value of the sum of both of your fractions is: &quot; &lt;&lt; decemal_output;<br />
}</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;using namespace std;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;FRACTION fraction;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Enter two fractions to have them multiplied together:&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// get fraction numerators and denominators<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cin &gt;&gt; fraction.numer_one;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; &quot; / &quot;;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cin &gt;&gt; fraction.denom_one;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; &quot; nAnd the other: n&quot;;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cin &gt;&gt; fraction.numer_two;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; &quot; / &quot;;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cin &gt;&gt; fraction.denom_two;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// call a function to output the sum of both fractions<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;fractionMultiplied(fraction);</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return 0;</p>
<p>}</p>
<p>/* END OF PROGRAMME */]</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
		<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 clearfix" id="comment-251948">
		<div id="div-comment-251948" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/850908eb9fef24070c4a33bbac182238?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/850908eb9fef24070c4a33bbac182238?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Jeremy</span>

		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/#comment-251948">

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/?replytocom=251948#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251948", "251948", "respond", "70" )' aria-label='Reply to Jeremy'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Are structure types generally defined outside all blocks (like a global variable)? This is the only thing I can&#8217;t seem to find an answer to. You obviously can declare them in blocks or functions, but is that bad style?</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-252056">
		<div id="div-comment-252056" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/87d25f970c178de6ce27ebf1d1001904?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/87d25f970c178de6ce27ebf1d1001904?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Janez</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/#comment-252056">
		April 4, 2015 at 1:03 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/?replytocom=252056#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252056", "252056", "respond", "70" )' aria-label='Reply to Janez'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Yes, they are (usually) defined outside all blocks. Since they are (user-defined) types, you want to access them from multiple functions (like you want to be able to declare variable of type int in multiple blocks).</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

<ul class="children">

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/47-structs/?replytocom=252417#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252417", "252417", "respond", "70" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>You mean in quiz 1?  Generally structs are useful for keeping related variables together in one place, both for organizational purposes, and because it makes it easier to code.</p>
<p>Any time you have two or more related non-trivial variables, you should consider putting them in a struct.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
